			"rendered": "<h3>Cloud-based Platform for Wi-Fi Device Management</h3>\n<p>Principal Interaction Designer in charge of UX for the company&#8217;s 6 interactive products:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Personal home/business wi-fi manager (iOS + Android) (now <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.cloudmondo.consumer\">blazeX</a>)</li>\n<li>Tablet-based Network Operation Center for cloud-managed wi-fi devices (iOS + Android) (now <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.cloudmondo.pocketNOQ\">blazeNOQ</a>)</li>\n<li>Web-based Network Operation Center for cloud-managed wi-fi devices (Web)</li>\n<li>Cloud-managed wi-fi device provisioning app  (Android)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>I was in charge of:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Understanding requirements from customers and stakeholders</li>\n<li>Translating business requirements and platform constrains into user-oriented and user-friendly interfaces</li>\n<li>Understanding the intricacies of the platform (easy set-up of cloud-based agent-managed &#8216;routers&#8217; by both technicians and end-users)</li>\n<li>Defining the workflows, screens, processes and interactions for the user interface</li>\n<li>Coordinating with the development team to get designs into production pipeline</li>\n<li>User-oriented and functionality QA control</li>\n<li>Management of the app&#8217;s online access points (Google Play Store / Apple App Store)</li>\n</ul>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-1 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-1 .gallery-item {\n\t\t\t\tfloat: left;\n\t\t\t\tmargin-top: both;' />\n\t</div>\n\n<blockquote><p><strong>Understanding and strategy</strong></p>\n<p>The first couple of weeks one visual designer and I interviewed all internal stakeholders and most of the developers to get a wide understanding of who we were targeting and what were we building.</p>\n<p>Then we made a workshop with all the stakeholders and engineers to discover the user flow hypotheses and create profiles of the personae hypotheses we wanted to test on the product. We also created hypotheses for the customer journeys we&#8217;d create in order to understand where to maximise value and where our platform will offer possible pain points.</p>\n<p>We also sat down with developers to understand in detail how the micro-services worked so we could have a good idea on how the experience worked on the backend and how that would affect the user experience. We created detailed flows of each process.</p></blockquote>\n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"2426\" />\n\t</div>\n\n<blockquote><p><strong>Designing the user flows</strong></p>\n<p>Next, I took a shot at the wireframes of the app, by first defining the user needs and goals and then defining a flow for each goal. I documented all the process on Confluence so developers had quick access to flows and screens and for the whole process to be easily updatable so we could move faster to the flows we would want to build.</p></blockquote>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-3 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-3 .gallery-item {\n\t\t\t\tfloat: left;\n\t\t\t\tmargin-top: Within a cadence of two-week sprints, we aim to have interface releases in every sprint, and immediately afterwards we tested them with real-life scenarios, and when possible, with real-life prospect customers.</p>\n<p>We managed to deliver all 6 apps within the 6-month deadline for a pilot programme abroad.</p></blockquote>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n",

			"rendered": "<h2>The role</h2>\n<p>I lead the UX and UI Direction for the final production of the GridOS for the Grid10 tablet and the Grid4 smartphone. My responsibilities included the overall interaction, information architecture and design direction for the final design process of the Grid Operative System (GridOS) and all native applications (messages, video, photos, video chat, address book, contextual menus, and filesystem) for the android-based <a title=\"Grid 10 Tablet\" href=\"http://www.engadget.com/2011/10/05/grid10-review/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Grid10 Tablet</a> and the  <a title=\"Grid 4 Touch Smartphone\" href=\"http://www.engadget.com/2011/08/16/hands-on-with-fusion-garages-grid-10-tablet-and-grid-4-smartpho/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Grid4 Smartphone</a>, managing a team of 7 graphic, motion-graphic and interaction designers.</p>\n<h2>The results</h2>\n<p>I helped transform a vision of an interface to be integrated on top of the Android OS into a robust, simple and usable interface. With a team of 5 Motion Graphic Designers and 2 Visual Designers I redesigned several of the existing applications (Photos, Videos, Messages, Calendar, Global Search, Notifications Centre and Contextual Menu) and designed others from scratch (&#8220;Chrome-less&#8221; Browser, Maps, Keyboard, Volume, Cross-device App AutoSync) working in extremely tight deadlines and an offshore development team based in Singapore and Southeast Asia.</p>\n<h2>The process</h2>\n<p>All deliveries were made in PSD files and very precise AfterEffects videos that described the interactions in great detail so development will perfectly align with the vision. We defined a workflow with no wireframes to interpret and understand, but instead we delivered videos that would tell a perfect story of the exact experience of the interaction with which users would be presented and delighted. We delivered in a tight cycle, getting specific business requirements every morning and delivering defined assets and guidance in a 24-to-48 hour iteration rounds.</p>\n<h2>The reviews</h2>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;The Grid software is clever and innovative in many ways&#8221;<br />\n&#8212; <a href=\"http://allthingsd.com/20111005/grid-10-tablet-hides-android-under-its-own-radical-design/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Walter Mossberg reviews the Grid 10 Tablet</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><a id=\"5b1764773f78a\" rel=\"wp-video-lightbox\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MZNaT8eq2CI&width=640&height=480\" title=\"\"><div 			"rendered": "Fullpipe Protective Snowboard Trousers (for Dainese)"

		"content": {
			"rendered": "<p>Design and production of a prototype set of snowboard trousers for the Bordercross xtreme snowboard speciality.</p>\n<p>The crossed stitching pattern allows the  protection pads to stay always in place, where the user needs them to be protected, while keeping 100% movability of the legs.</p>\n<p>Produced in 2000-2003 by Dainese as Valdez/Laax pants, currently inspiring many of Dainese <a href=\"http://www.dainese.com/us_en/catalog/product/view/id/96816/s/egemone-d-dry-pants/\">competitive snowboard trouser collections</a>.</p>\n\n\t\t<style
